## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / batch reactor ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A in time t, which is the standard setting for kinetic rate laws. With only A and t available, the most likely models are single-species consumption/production ODEs (orders, saturation, equilibrium approach, or time-varying effective rate constants).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics (constant consumption/production): dA_dt = c0 (rate independent of A, e.g., surface-limited or constant feed/removal)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; well-mixed batch consumption)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or dimerization-like consumption in terms of A only)
- General nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate order fitting)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Affine source+sink (production minus first-order loss): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant generation with linear depletion)
- Saturating (capacity-limited) rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate becomes ~constant at high A, ~first-order at low A)
- Inhibited/limited at high concentration: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (self-inhibition or crowding/transport limitation in an effective 1-variable form)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating then self-limiting dynamics; sigmoidal A(t))
- Mixed-order polynomial rate law: dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2) (parallel first- and second-order pathways lumped)
- Stretched-exponential (time-dependent deactivation) effective first order: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or transient availability causing k(t) to decay)
- Activation/induction period effective first order: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (catalyst activation, heating ramp captured phenomenologically as increasing k(t))
- Power-law time-varying rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A (ageing/activation effects with algebraic k(t))
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (light/duty-cycle forcing or oscillatory environment affecting effective rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production sign: for a decaying reactant A, expect dA_dt <= 0 for A > 0; persistent positive dA_dt suggests net generation or relaxation to higher equilibrium.
- Reaction order fingerprint: if dA_dt scales like A, A**2, or A**c, then plotting log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) is approximately linear with slope near the order.
- Equilibrium approach: a nonzero steady state A* is suggested when dA_dt crosses zero near A ≈ c1, consistent with dA_dt ∝ -(A-c1) or c0-c1*A.
- Parallel pathways: curvature that cannot be fit by a single power A**c often indicates sums like (c0*A + c1*A**2) or other additive rate contributions.
- Saturation/transport limitation: if |dA_dt| increases with A at low A but plateaus at high A, rational forms like A/(A+c1) are typical (finite capacity/limited sites).
- Autocatalysis signature: if rate is small at very low A, increases at intermediate A, then decreases near a maximum A, a product form like A*(c1-A) captures the bell-shaped rate vs A.
- Time-varying kinetics: systematic drift in rate at the same A value across different t indicates k(t) dependence (multiplicative exp(±c*t) or (t+c1)**c2 factors).
- Periodic forcing: oscillations in dA_dt at roughly fixed A suggest explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) modulation of an underlying rate law.
- Physical admissibility: concentration models typically require A >= 0; rate laws that can drive A negative without a stabilizing term may be nonphysical unless the data range avoids that regime.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)**

Key features of GT:
- An A² term
- A sin(√A) term
- No dependence on t
- No other terms

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. For a candidate to match, it must:
1. Be expressible as c*A² + d*sin(√A) (possibly with constant offsets that can be zeroed)
2. Have no t-dependence (or t-dependent terms must be eliminable)

Many candidates have the form: `sqrt(A)*c0*exp(A*c1) + A²*c2 + A*c3 + ...`

The key question is: can `sqrt(A)*exp(A*c1)` equal `sin(√A)`? 

No! `sqrt(A)*exp(A*c1)` is an exponential-type function, while `sin(√A)` is oscillatory. Even with c1=0, we'd get `c0*sqrt(A)`, which is not sin(√A). These are fundamentally different basis functions. So any candidate relying on `sqrt(A)*exp(A*c1)` to produce the sin(√A) term cannot match.

Similarly, rational functions of A, polynomials in A, log terms, etc., cannot produce sin(√A).

Let me check candidates that might contain sin(√A) or equivalent:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*sqrt(A²+c1) + c2*|A|^c3 + c4*(|A|^c5+1)^c6 + c7` - No sin term. Cannot match. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates 2-72, and most others:** Most contain `sqrt(A)*c0*exp(A*c1)` or polynomial/rational terms. None contain sin(√A).

Let me specifically look for any candidate with a sin term that could become sin(√A):

- **Candidate 2:** sin(c6*t + c7) - this is sin of t, not sin(√A). Setting c6=0 gives a constant. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 3:** sin(c6 + c7*t) - same issue. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 11:** sin(c5*t + c6) - t-dependent sin. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 44:** sin(A*c6 + c7) - sin of linear A, not sin(√A). [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 45:** sin(c6*log(c7*|A|+1) + c8) - sin(log(...)), not sin(√A). [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 50:** sin(A*c5 + c6) - sin of linear A. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 59:** sin(c6*t + c7) - t-dependent. [NO MATCH]

None of the candidates contain sin(√A) as a basis function. The function sin(√A) cannot be represented by any combination of:
- Polynomials in A
- exp(A*c)
- sqrt(A)*exp(A*c)
- sin(linear in A or t)
- log terms
- Rational functions of A
- |A|^c terms
- sqrt(A²+c) terms
